PHASE I

1. ABOUT THE PROJECT

1.I Introduction

The Smart Restaurant Management System is a modern, full-stack web application designed to digitize and streamline the complete restaurant operations -- from order placement to delivery, table reservation, payment processing, and customer engagement. Built using the MERN stack (MongoDB, Express.js, React.js, Node.js), this application serves as a comprehensive digital platform for both customers and restaurant administrators.

In today's fast-paced digital era, the food industry is rapidly shifting towards online and contactless solutions. Traditional methods of managing a restaurant -- such as manual order-taking, paper-based reservations, and cash-only payments -- are no longer efficient or scalable. This project addresses these challenges by providing an integrated web-based solution that handles everything from browsing the menu to making payments, tracking orders in real-time, and managing loyalty programs.

The system comprises two major interfaces:

  • Customer Interface: A visually rich, responsive frontend where customers can browse the menu, add items to cart, apply coupons, make online payments via Razorpay, track their orders in real-time, book tables, manage favourites, earn loyalty points, use a digital wallet, refer friends, write reviews, and chat with support.
  • Admin Panel: A protected dashboard for restaurant administrators to manage menu items, view analytics, handle orders, manage coupons and flash deals, respond to customer chat queries, and manage table reservations.

The frontend is developed using React 19 with Vite as the build tool and Tailwind CSS for styling, while the backend runs on Node.js with Express.js and uses MongoDB Atlas as the cloud database. The system also integrates Razorpay for secure payment processing and Nodemailer for OTP-based email authentication.

1.II Objective

The primary objectives of this project are:

  1. Digitize Restaurant Operations: Replace manual and paper-based processes with an automated, web-based system for order management, menu handling, table reservations, and customer engagement.
  2. Enhance Customer Experience: Provide customers with a seamless, fast, and visually appealing interface for browsing the menu, placing orders, making payments, and tracking deliveries in real-time.
  3. Enable Secure Online Payments: Integrate Razorpay payment gateway for secure, hassle-free online payment processing with order verification.
  4. Implement Real-Time Order Tracking: Allow customers to track their orders through a 6-stage visual pipeline -- Pending, then Confirmed, then Preparing, then Out for Delivery, and finally Delivered (or Rejected).
  5. Build a Loyalty and Rewards Ecosystem: Implement loyalty points (1 point per Rs.1 spent), a 4-tier reward system (Bronze, Silver, Gold, Platinum), a digital wallet with transaction history, and a referral program (Rs.100 bonus for both referrer and referee).
  6. Provide Admin Control Panel: Give administrators a comprehensive dashboard to manage menu items (CRUD), create/manage coupons and flash deals, view analytics and revenue data, manage table bookings, and handle customer support chat.
  7. Ensure Security and Authentication: Implement JWT-based token authentication, OTP-based email verification for registration, password hashing with bcryptjs, and API rate limiting to prevent abuse.
  8. Offer Advanced Menu Discovery: Enable advanced filtering by category, price range, rating, dietary preferences (veg/non-veg, vegan, gluten-free), spice level, and text-based search with sorting options.
  9. Support Mobile-First Design: Build a responsive, Progressive Web App (PWA) with mobile bottom navigation, service worker support, and touch-friendly UI for optimal mobile experience.
  10. Create Scalable Architecture: Design a modular, REST API-based architecture that can scale to handle increasing numbers of users, orders, and menu items without significant refactoring.

2. PRELIMINARY INVESTIGATION

2.I Tools/Platform Used

The "Smart Restaurant Management System" project was developed using full-stack web development tools and frameworks. Each tool played an important role in creating a secure and feature-rich system.

1. Core Technologies

  • MERN Stack: MERN stack provides a complete development environment for web applications. React (v19.0.0) is used for frontend UI, Node.js and Express (v4.21.2) are used for backend API services, and MongoDB is used for storing application data.
  • MongoDB Atlas (Database): A cloud-hosted NoSQL database that stores all entities such as Users, Menu Items, Orders, Reservations, Coupons, Flash Deals, Reviews, Feedback, Favourites, Chat Messages, Loyalty Points, Wallets, Referrals, and Settings. It is a document-oriented database that stores data in flexible, JSON-like BSON format.
  • Express.js (Backend Framework, v4.21.2): A minimal and flexible Node.js web application framework that creates REST APIs for authentication, menu management, order processing, payment verification, reservation handling, coupon management, and all other backend operations.
  • React.js (Frontend, v19.0.0): A JavaScript library for building interactive and responsive user interfaces. It is used with Vite (v6.0.5) as the build tool for fast development and optimized production builds. React builds both the Customer interface and the Admin dashboard.
  • Node.js (Backend Runtime, v18+): A JavaScript runtime built on Chrome's V8 engine that allows JavaScript to run on the server side. It handles all backend logic, API routing, database operations, and third-party integrations.

2. Frontend Technologies

  • Vite (v6.0.5): A next-generation frontend build tool that provides extremely fast Hot Module Replacement (HMR) during development and optimized bundling for production. It replaces traditional tools like Webpack.
  • Tailwind CSS (v3.4.17): A utility-first CSS framework that allows rapid UI development by composing styles directly in HTML/JSX using utility classes. It eliminates the need for writing custom CSS files for most styling needs.
  • Framer Motion (v11.15.0): A production-ready animation library for React that provides declarative animations, page transitions, and gesture-based interactions with minimal code.
  • React Router DOM (v7.1.1): The standard routing library for React applications that enables client-side navigation between pages without full page reloads.
  • Axios (v1.7.9): A promise-based HTTP client for making API requests from the frontend to the backend. It supports request/response interceptors, automatic JSON parsing, and error handling.
  • Lucide React (v0.468.0): A lightweight, customizable icon library that provides clean SVG icons used throughout the application for navigation, actions, and visual indicators.
  • React Hot Toast (v2.4.1): A lightweight toast notification library that provides instant visual feedback for user actions like adding items to cart, applying coupons, placing orders, and error messages.

3. Authentication and Security Technologies

  • JWT (JSON Web Token, v9.0.2): Used for stateless authentication and session management. After successful login, a JWT token is generated with a 7-day expiry and stored in the browser's localStorage. Every protected API request includes this token in the Authorization header.
  • bcryptjs (v2.4.3): Used to hash and verify user passwords securely. Passwords are never stored in plain text -- they are hashed using bcrypt's one-way hashing algorithm with salt rounds before storing in the database.
  • Express Rate Limit (v8.3.2): Used to throttle API requests to prevent brute-force attacks and abuse. General API endpoints are limited to 100 requests per 15 minutes, while authentication endpoints are limited to 10 requests per 15 minutes.

4. Email and OTP Tools

  • Nodemailer (v6.9.16): Used for sending emails via Gmail SMTP. It handles OTP delivery for registration and login, order confirmation emails with detailed item lists and bill summary, and login success notification emails.
  • OTP System: A custom 6-digit OTP system is implemented using Node.js crypto module. OTPs are stored in MongoDB with a TTL (Time-To-Live) index that automatically deletes expired OTPs after 5 minutes.

5. Payment and Integration Tools

  • Razorpay SDK (v2.9.5): India's leading payment gateway integrated for secure online payment processing. It supports UPI, credit/debit cards, net banking, and wallet payments. The integration includes order creation, payment verification using HMAC SHA256 signature, and webhook handling.

6. Development and Deployment Tools

  • Nodemon (v3.1.9): A development utility that automatically restarts the Node.js server whenever file changes are detected, improving development workflow.
  • ESLint (v9.17.0): A JavaScript linting tool that enforces code quality and consistency across the codebase.
  • PostCSS (v8.4.49) + Autoprefixer (v10.4.20): CSS processing tools that add vendor prefixes for cross-browser compatibility.
  • Vercel: A cloud hosting platform used for deploying both the frontend and serverless backend functions. It provides automatic HTTPS, CI/CD pipelines, global CDN, and free tier hosting.
  • Git: Version control system used for source code management and collaboration.
  • Visual Studio Code: The primary code editor used for development with extensions for React, ESLint, Tailwind CSS IntelliSense, and Thunder Client for API testing.
  • Chrome DevTools: Used for debugging, performance profiling, network monitoring, and responsive design testing.

2.II Hardware/Software Requirements

Hardware Requirements (Development and Testing):

  • Processor: Minimum Intel Core i3 or AMD Ryzen 3. Recommended Intel Core i5 or AMD Ryzen 5 or above for smooth development experience.
  • RAM: Minimum 4 GB. Recommended 8 GB or above for running multiple development tools simultaneously.
  • Storage: Minimum 10 GB free disk space. Recommended 20 GB SSD for faster build times and development server startup.
  • Display: Minimum 1366 x 768 resolution. Recommended 1920 x 1080 or above for comfortable coding and UI testing.
  • Internet: Broadband internet connection is required for MongoDB Atlas cloud database access, Razorpay payment gateway, Nodemailer email service, npm package installation, and deployment to Vercel.

Software Requirements:

  • Operating System: Windows 10/11, macOS 12+, or Ubuntu 20.04+ (any OS that supports Node.js)
  • Node.js: Version 18.x or above (JavaScript runtime for server-side programming)
  • npm: Version 9.x or above (Node Package Manager for dependency management)
  • Web Browser: Google Chrome 100+, Firefox 100+, or Microsoft Edge 100+ (for testing and debugging)
  • Code Editor: Visual Studio Code (recommended) with React and Tailwind CSS extensions
  • Database: MongoDB Atlas (cloud-hosted) -- no local database installation needed
  • Git: Version 2.30 or above for version control and source code management

Deployment Requirements:

  • Frontend Hosting: Vercel free tier -- provides automatic builds, HTTPS, and global CDN
  • Backend Hosting: Vercel Serverless Functions -- runs Express.js as serverless API
  • Database: MongoDB Atlas Free Tier -- provides 512 MB storage with automatic backups
  • Domain: Custom domain is optional -- Vercel provides free .vercel.app subdomain
  • SSL Certificate: Auto-provisioned by Vercel (HTTPS enabled by default)

3. FEASIBILITY STUDY

3.I Operational Feasibility

The Smart Restaurant Management System is operationally feasible because:

  1. User-Friendly Interface: The application uses a modern, visually appealing design built with Tailwind CSS and Framer Motion animations. Customers can easily browse the menu, add items to cart, and place orders with minimal effort. The dark-themed UI with amber accents provides a premium dining feel.
  2. Minimal Training Required: The customer-facing application follows standard e-commerce patterns (browse menu, add to cart, checkout, pay) that are familiar to most internet users. The admin panel uses intuitive CRUD interfaces with clear labels and actions.
  3. Multiple Access Points: The system is accessible via any modern web browser (Chrome, Firefox, Edge, Safari) on desktops, tablets, and mobile devices. The PWA support with service worker enables app-like experience on mobile.
  4. Real-Time Feedback: The system provides immediate feedback for every action -- toast notifications for cart updates, visual order tracking timeline, flash deal countdowns, and live chat support.
  5. Existing Workflow Compatibility: The system mirrors the actual restaurant workflow -- customers browse menu, place orders, make payments; admins receive orders, update status, manage inventory. This reduces resistance to adoption.
  6. Low Maintenance Overhead: With cloud-hosted database (MongoDB Atlas) and serverless deployment (Vercel), the system requires minimal server maintenance. Auto-scaling handles traffic spikes.

3.II Technical Feasibility

The project is technically feasible due to the following factors:

  1. Proven Technology Stack: The MERN stack (MongoDB, Express.js, React.js, Node.js) is one of the most widely used and well-documented full-stack JavaScript frameworks. All technologies used are open-source, actively maintained, and battle-tested at scale.
  2. Cloud Infrastructure: MongoDB Atlas provides a managed, scalable database with automatic backups, monitoring, and a generous free tier (512 MB). Vercel provides free hosting with automatic HTTPS, CI/CD pipelines, and global CDN.
  3. Third-Party Integration: Razorpay provides a well-documented Node.js SDK for payment processing with test/sandbox mode for development. Nodemailer provides reliable email service using Gmail SMTP for OTP delivery. Both services have free tiers suitable for development and small-scale production.
  4. Security Implementation: JWT provides stateless authentication with 7-day token expiry. bcryptjs provides one-way password hashing. Express Rate Limit provides 100 requests per 15 minutes for general API and 10 requests per 15 minutes for auth endpoints. OTP auto-deletion with MongoDB TTL index ensures expired OTPs are automatically removed.
  5. Modular Architecture: The codebase follows a clean separation of concerns -- Models, Routes, Middleware, Context Providers, Pages, and Components are all organized in separate directories, making the code maintainable and extensible.
  6. Development Tooling: Vite provides near-instant hot module replacement (HMR) for frontend development. Nodemon auto-restarts the server on changes. ESLint enforces code quality.

3.III Economic Feasibility

The project is economically feasible for the following reasons:

  • Development Tools -- Rs.0 (Free): Visual Studio Code, Node.js, React.js, Express.js, Tailwind CSS, and all other development tools used are completely free and open-source. No licensing costs are involved.
  • Database -- Rs.0 (Free Tier): MongoDB Atlas free tier provides 512 MB of database storage, which is sufficient for development, testing, and small-scale production deployment.
  • Hosting -- Rs.0 (Free Tier): Vercel free tier includes 100 GB bandwidth per month, serverless function execution, automatic HTTPS, and CI/CD pipelines. This is sufficient for hosting both frontend and backend.
  • Payment Gateway -- 2% per transaction: Razorpay charges only per successful transaction. There is no setup fee, no monthly fee, and no minimum transaction requirement. The test/sandbox mode is completely free.
  • Email Service -- Rs.0 (Free): Gmail SMTP via Nodemailer provides up to 500 emails per day for free, which is sufficient for OTP delivery, order confirmations, and login notifications.
  • Domain Name -- Rs.500-1000/year: This is optional. Vercel provides a free .vercel.app subdomain that can be used for deployment.
  • SSL Certificate -- Rs.0 (Free): SSL is auto-provisioned by Vercel, so HTTPS is enabled by default at no cost.
  • Total Initial Cost -- Rs.0 to Rs.1,000: The entire system can be developed and deployed with zero to minimal upfront cost, making it highly economically feasible.

Return on Investment:

  • Reduced manual order errors leading to improved customer satisfaction
  • Online payment processing enabling faster transactions and reduced cash handling
  • Loyalty and referral programs increasing customer retention and acquisition
  • Digital menu management enabling instant price/item updates without reprinting
  • Analytics dashboard enabling data-driven business decisions

4. INFORMATION GATHERING

4.I On-site Observation

The following observations were made by visiting local restaurants and food delivery platforms:

  1. Order Management: Most small-to-medium restaurants still rely on manual order-taking via phone calls or in-person visits. This leads to miscommunication, delayed orders, and difficulty in tracking order status.
  2. Menu Updates: Physical menu cards are expensive to reprint when prices change or items are added/removed. Many restaurants use WhatsApp or social media to share daily specials, which is unorganized.
  3. Payment Processing: Cash-on-delivery is still dominant in smaller restaurants. Customers increasingly prefer digital payments (UPI, cards), but many restaurants lack integrated payment systems.
  4. Table Reservations: Most restaurants handle reservations via phone calls with no confirmation system. This leads to double bookings and no-shows.
  5. Customer Feedback: Feedback is rarely collected systematically. Restaurants rely on Google Reviews or verbal feedback, missing valuable insights.
  6. Loyalty Programs: Very few local restaurants have loyalty programs. Those that do use physical stamp cards, which are easily lost or forgotten.

4.II Questionnaire

A questionnaire was distributed to 50 potential users (restaurant customers and 5 restaurant owners) with the following key findings:

Customer Responses (45 respondents):

When asked "Do you prefer ordering food online?", 89% respondents said Yes while 11% said No. For the question "Would you use a real-time order tracking feature?", 93% said Yes and 7% said No. Regarding "Do you value loyalty/reward programs?", 78% said Yes and 22% said No. When asked "Would you use digital wallet for restaurant payments?", 67% said Yes and 33% said No. For "Do you read reviews before ordering a new dish?", 84% said Yes and 16% said No. Regarding "Would you refer friends for a bonus reward?", 72% said Yes and 28% said No. Finally, "Do you prefer advanced filtering (veg/non-veg, spice level)?" received 91% Yes and 9% No responses.

Restaurant Owner Responses (5 respondents):

When asked "Do you face order management challenges?", 100% said Yes. For "Would you use a digital menu management system?", 80% said Yes and 20% said No. Regarding "Is analytics/reporting important for your business?", 100% said Yes. When asked "Would you like automated coupon/deal management?", 80% said Yes and 20% said No. For "Do you need a customer chat support system?", 60% said Yes and 40% said No.

4.III Interview

Interviews were conducted with 3 restaurant managers and 10 frequent food-ordering customers:

Key Insights from Restaurant Managers:

  1. Peak hours create chaos in order management -- a digital system with order queue would help significantly.
  2. They want to run time-limited flash deals during slow hours to increase footfall.
  3. Customer data (order history, preferences) would help in personalizing services.
  4. They need a simple admin interface -- not overly complex.
  5. Real-time chat would reduce phone calls during busy hours.

Key Insights from Customers:

  1. Order tracking is the most desired feature -- knowing exactly when food will arrive reduces anxiety.
  2. Coupons and discounts are strong motivators for choosing a platform.
  3. A clean, fast-loading mobile experience is non-negotiable.
  4. Review system helps in trying new dishes with confidence.
  5. Combo deals offer better value -- customers actively seek them.

6.II Data Dictionary

User Collection:

  • _id (ObjectId, Primary Key, Auto-generated): Unique identifier for each user.
  • name (String, Required): User's full name.
  • email (String, Required, Unique): User's email address used for authentication and communication.
  • password (String, Required, Hashed with bcryptjs): Encrypted password stored as a one-way hash.
  • role (String, Default: "user"): User role which can be "user" or "admin".
  • createdAt (Date, Auto-generated): Timestamp of account creation.
  • updatedAt (Date, Auto-generated): Timestamp of last profile update.

Order Collection:

  • _id (ObjectId, Primary Key): Unique order identifier.
  • name (String, Required): Customer's name for delivery.
  • email (String, Required): Customer's email for order confirmation and tracking.
  • phone (String, Required): Contact phone number.
  • address (String, Required): Full delivery address with landmark.
  • items (Array, Required): Array of ordered items, each containing name (String), price (Number), quantity (Number), image (String), extras (Array of Strings for add-ons), and spiceLevel (String).
  • totalAmount (Number, Required): Total order amount in INR.
  • status (String, Enum): Current order status which can be Pending, Confirmed, Preparing, Out for Delivery, Delivered, or Rejected. Default is "Pending".
  • createdAt / updatedAt (Date): Auto-generated timestamps.

Menu Collection:

  • _id (ObjectId, Primary Key): Unique item identifier.
  • name (String, Required): Dish name.
  • price (Number, Required): Price in INR.
  • description (String): Detailed dish description.
  • image (String): Image URL for the dish.
  • category (String, Default: "Other"): Food category such as Starters, Main Course, Rice and Biryani, Breads, Chinese, Fast Food, Beverages, or Desserts.
  • available (Boolean, Default: true): Whether the item is currently available for ordering.
  • isVeg (Boolean, Default: true): Vegetarian flag.
  • rating (Number, Default: 4.0): Average customer rating.
  • bestseller (Boolean, Default: false): Whether the item is marked as a bestseller.

Coupon Collection:

  • code (String, Required, Unique, Uppercase): Coupon code like WELCOME20, LACASA50.
  • discount (Number, Required): Discount value (percentage or flat amount).
  • type (String, Enum: "percent" or "flat"): Type of discount.
  • minOrder (Number, Default: 0): Minimum order amount required to apply the coupon.
  • maxDiscount (Number, Default: 0): Maximum discount cap for percentage coupons.
  • description (String): Human-readable coupon description.
  • active (Boolean, Default: true): Whether the coupon is currently active.
  • usageLimit (Number, Default: 0): Maximum number of times the coupon can be used. 0 means unlimited.
  • usedCount (Number, Default: 0): Number of times the coupon has been used.
  • expiresAt (Date): Expiry date of the coupon.

Loyalty Points Collection:

  • userId (ObjectId, FK to User, Unique): Linked user.
  • totalPoints (Number, Default: 0): Total points ever earned.
  • usedPoints (Number, Default: 0): Points redeemed so far.
  • availablePoints (Number, Default: 0): Currently available points for redemption.
  • tier (String, Enum: Bronze, Silver, Gold, Platinum): Current loyalty tier based on total points.
  • tier_progress (Number, Default: 0): Progress percentage towards next tier.
  • pointHistory (Array): Array of point transactions with type, amount, description, and date.

Wallet Collection:

  • userId (ObjectId, FK to User, Unique): Linked user.
  • balance (Number, Default: 0): Current wallet balance in INR.
  • transactionHistory (Array): Array of credit/debit transactions.
  • totalCredit (Number, Default: 0): Total money ever added to wallet.
  • totalDebit (Number, Default: 0): Total money ever spent from wallet.

Referral Collection:

  • referrerId (ObjectId, FK to User): User who generates the referral.
  • referralCode (String, Unique, Required): Unique referral code.
  • referredUsers (Array): List of users who signed up using this referral code.
  • bonusAmount (Number, Default: 100): Bonus amount in Rs. given per successful referral.
  • totalBonusEarned (Number, Default: 0): Total referral bonus earned.
  • totalReferrals (Number, Default: 0): Count of successful referrals.

Review Collection:

  • menuItemId (ObjectId, FK to Menu, Required): The menu item being reviewed.
  • userId (ObjectId, FK to User, Required): The user who wrote the review.
  • userName (String): Display name of the reviewer.
  • rating (Number, Min: 1, Max: 5, Required): Star rating.
  • title (String): Review headline.
  • comment (String): Detailed review text.
  • images (Array of Strings): URLs of review images.
  • helpful (Number, Default: 0): Count of "helpful" votes from other users.
  • verified (Boolean, Default: false): Whether the reviewer has a verified purchase.

Reservation Collection:

  • name (String, Required): Guest name.
  • phone (String, Required): Contact phone number.
  • guests (Number, Required): Number of guests.
  • date (String, Required): Reservation date.
  • time (String, Required): Reservation time.
  • status (String, Default: "Pending"): Booking status.

Flash Deal Collection:

  • title (String, Required): Deal title displayed on the banner.
  • description (String): Deal description.
  • discountPercent (Number, Required): Discount percentage offered.
  • menuItems (Array of Strings): IDs of applicable menu items.
  • startTime (String, Required): Start time in HH:mm format.
  • endTime (String, Required): End time in HH:mm format.
  • daysOfWeek (Array of Numbers): Active days where 0=Sunday, 1=Monday through 6=Saturday. Empty array means every day.
  • active (Boolean, Default: true): Whether the deal is currently active.

Chat Message Collection:

  • conversationId (String, Required, Indexed): Unique chat thread identifier.
  • sender (String, Enum: "user" or "admin"): Who sent the message.
  • senderEmail (String): Email of the sender.
  • message (String, Required): Message content.
  • read (Boolean, Default: false): Whether the message has been read.

Feedback Collection:

  • orderId (String, Required, Unique): Linked order ID (one feedback per order).
  • email (String, Required): Customer's email.
  • rating (Number, Min: 1, Max: 5, Required): Overall experience rating.
  • comment (String): Feedback text.
  • deliveryRating (Number, Min: 1, Max: 5): Delivery experience rating.
  • foodRating (Number, Min: 1, Max: 5): Food quality rating.

OTP Collection:

  • email (String, Required): Email address for OTP delivery.
  • otp (String, Required): 6-digit OTP code.
  • purpose (String, Required): Purpose of OTP -- either "register" or "login".
  • name (String): User's name (only for registration OTPs).
  • password (String): Hashed password (only for registration OTPs).
  • expiresAt (Date, Required): Expiry time (5 minutes from creation). MongoDB TTL index automatically deletes expired documents.

Settings Collection:

  • restaurantName (String, Default: "LaCasa"): Restaurant name.
  • address (String): Restaurant address.
  • phone (String): Contact phone.
  • email (String): Contact email.
  • openingTime (String, Default: "10:00 AM"): Opening time.
  • closingTime (String, Default: "11:00 PM"): Closing time.
  • taxPercent (Number, Default: 5): Tax percentage applied to orders.
  • deliveryCharge (Number, Default: 0): Delivery charge in INR.

7.II Database Design

The application uses MongoDB Atlas (cloud-hosted NoSQL database) with Mongoose ODM (v8.9.5). MongoDB stores data in flexible, JSON-like BSON documents, making it ideal for the varied data structures in this application.

The database contains the following 17 collections:

  • users: Stores user accounts with name, email, hashed password, and role.
  • orders: Stores all orders with customer details, ordered items, total amount, and status.
  • menus: Stores menu items with name, price, description, image, category, availability, veg/non-veg flag, rating, and bestseller flag.
  • reservations: Stores table reservations with guest details, date, time, and status.
  • reviews: Stores item reviews with rating, comments, and images.
  • feedbacks: Stores post-order feedback with overall, food, and delivery ratings.
  • otps: Stores temporary OTPs with TTL auto-deletion after 5 minutes.
  • coupons: Stores discount coupons with code, type, limits, and expiry.
  • flashdeals: Stores time-limited deals with schedule and applicable items.
  • favourites: Stores user favourites with compound index on email + menuItemId.
  • chatmessages: Stores chat messages with conversation threading.
  • settings: Stores restaurant configuration (single document).
  • tables: Stores QR-enabled table configurations.
  • wallets: Stores user wallet balances and transaction history.
  • loyaltypoints: Stores user loyalty points, tier, and point history.
  • referrals: Stores referral codes and referred user lists.
  • combos: Stores combo deal configurations.

8. PROCESS DESIGN

8.I Authentication Flow

The system uses a two-step OTP-based authentication flow for both registration and login:

Registration Process:

  1. User enters name, email, and password on the Register page.
  2. Frontend sends POST request to /api/auth/register/send-otp with user details.
  3. Backend validates input, checks if user already exists, hashes the password using bcryptjs.
  4. Backend generates a 6-digit OTP using Node.js crypto module.
  5. OTP is stored in MongoDB OTP collection with 5-minute TTL (auto-deletion).
  6. OTP is emailed to the user via Nodemailer using Gmail SMTP.
  7. User enters the 6-digit OTP in the UI (6 individual input boxes with auto-focus).
  8. Frontend sends POST request to /api/auth/register/verify-otp with email and OTP.
  9. Backend verifies OTP matches and is not expired.
  10. User account is created in the database with hashed password.
  11. JWT token is generated with 7-day expiry and returned to frontend.
  12. Token and user data are stored in localStorage.
  13. User is redirected to the home page.

Login Process:

  1. User enters email and password on the Login page.
  2. Frontend sends POST to /api/auth/login/send-otp.
  3. Backend finds user by email, verifies password with bcrypt.compare.
  4. If credentials are valid, a 6-digit OTP is generated and stored with 5-minute TTL.
  5. OTP is emailed to the user.
  6. User enters OTP in the verification form.
  7. Frontend sends POST to /api/auth/login/verify-otp.
  8. Backend verifies OTP, generates JWT token, and sends a login success email.
  9. Token and user data stored in localStorage, user redirected to previous page or home.

8.II Order Processing Flow

The order processing follows this flow:

  1. Customer browses the menu and adds items to cart using the CartContext state manager.
  2. Customer proceeds to checkout page (requires authentication -- redirects to login if not logged in).
  3. Customer fills in delivery details: name, email, phone (10-digit validation), and address.
  4. Customer can optionally apply a coupon code for discount.
  5. Bill is calculated: Subtotal + 5% Tax + Delivery Charge - Coupon Discount = Grand Total.
  6. Customer clicks "Place Order" which sends POST to /api/orders.
  7. Backend creates order document in MongoDB with status "Pending".
  8. Order confirmation email is sent to customer with detailed item list and bill summary.
  9. Order appears in Admin Dashboard with real-time polling (every 3 seconds).
  10. Admin can update order status through the pipeline: Pending, Confirmed, Preparing, Out for Delivery, Delivered. Admin can also Reject an order.
  11. Customer can track order status in real-time on the Tracking page.

8.III Payment Processing Flow (Razorpay)

The payment processing uses Razorpay payment gateway:

  1. When customer chooses online payment, frontend sends POST to /api/payment/create-order with amount.
  2. Backend converts amount to paise (multiplied by 100) and calls razorpay.orders.create() with amount, currency "INR", and a receipt ID.
  3. Razorpay returns an order ID which is sent back to the frontend.
  4. Frontend opens Razorpay checkout widget with the order ID, amount, and restaurant details.
  5. Customer completes payment through Razorpay (UPI, card, net banking, or wallet).
  6. On successful payment, Razorpay sends payment_id, order_id, and signature to the frontend callback.
  7. Frontend sends these three values to POST /api/payment/verify.
  8. Backend verifies the signature using HMAC SHA256 with the Razorpay key secret.
  9. If signature is valid, payment is confirmed and order is placed.

8.IV Table Reservation Flow

  1. Customer fills in reservation form: name, phone, number of guests, date, and time.
  2. Frontend sends POST to /api/reservations with the reservation details.
  3. Backend validates all required fields and creates a reservation document with status "Pending".
  4. Reservation appears in Admin Dashboard under the "Table Reservations" tab.
  5. Admin can Confirm or Cancel the reservation.
  6. Admin can also Delete reservations that are no longer needed.

8.V Coupon and Flash Deal System

Coupon Flow:

  1. Admin creates coupons from Admin Coupon Management page with code, discount type (flat/percent), minimum order, maximum discount, usage limit, and expiry date.
  2. On the Checkout page, customer can apply a coupon code manually or select from the "View available coupons" list.
  3. System validates the coupon: checks if code exists, is active, has not exceeded usage limit, is not expired, and minimum order amount is met.
  4. If valid, discount is calculated and applied to the order total.

Flash Deal Flow:

  1. Admin creates flash deals with title, discount percentage, start/end time, and active days.
  2. When a flash deal is active (current time is between start and end time on an active day), a countdown banner appears at the top of the customer interface.
  3. The banner shows deal title, discount, and a live countdown timer to the deal's end time.

9. TESTING

9.I Testing Strategy

The Smart Restaurant Management System was tested using a combination of manual testing methodologies to ensure all features work correctly, the user interface is responsive, and edge cases are handled properly.

9.II Unit Testing

Individual components and API endpoints were tested in isolation:

  • Authentication APIs: Tested registration with valid/invalid inputs, duplicate email handling, OTP generation and verification, expired OTP handling, login with correct/incorrect credentials, and JWT token generation.
  • Order APIs: Tested order creation with valid/missing fields, order status updates through all pipeline stages, order deletion, and email notification sending.
  • Menu APIs: Tested CRUD operations (create, read, update, delete), availability toggle, menu seeding, and category filtering.
  • Payment APIs: Tested Razorpay order creation, payment verification with valid/invalid signatures.
  • Reservation APIs: Tested reservation creation, status updates, and deletion.
  • Coupon APIs: Tested coupon creation, validation logic, minimum order checks, usage limits, and expiry handling.
  • Cart Context: Tested addToCart, removeFromCart, increaseQty, decreaseQty, clearCart, and totalPrice calculation.

9.III Integration Testing

End-to-end user flows were tested to ensure all components work together:

  • Complete Order Flow: Browse menu, add items to cart, proceed to checkout, fill delivery details, apply coupon, place order, verify order in admin dashboard, update status, check order tracking on customer side.
  • Authentication Flow: Register new account with OTP verification, login with OTP, verify token persistence across page refreshes, test logout and protected route redirects.
  • Payment Flow: Complete checkout, initiate Razorpay payment, complete payment in test mode, verify payment confirmation and order creation.
  • Admin Flow: Login as admin, manage menu items (add/edit/delete), create coupons, manage flash deals, update order status, respond to customer chats.

9.IV UI/UX Testing

  • Responsive Design: Tested on desktop (1920x1080), tablet (768x1024), and mobile (375x812) viewports. Verified mobile bottom navigation, hamburger menu, and touch-friendly controls.
  • Browser Compatibility: Tested on Google Chrome, Mozilla Firefox, Microsoft Edge, and Safari.
  • Animation Performance: Verified Framer Motion animations run smoothly without jank on page transitions, cart updates, and modal popups.
  • Dark Theme: Verified all text is readable against the dark background, amber accent colors are consistent, and all interactive elements have visible hover/focus states.

9.V Security Testing

  • Authentication: Verified JWT tokens expire after 7 days, invalid tokens return 403 error, and protected routes redirect to login.
  • Rate Limiting: Verified API returns 429 "Too Many Requests" after exceeding rate limits (100 general, 10 auth).
  • Input Validation: Tested SQL injection and XSS attempts on all input fields. HTML content in order data is escaped using escapeHtml() function.
  • Password Security: Verified passwords are stored as bcrypt hashes, never in plain text.
  • OTP Security: Verified OTPs expire after 5 minutes, old OTPs are deleted when new ones are generated, and invalid OTPs are rejected.

10. MAINTENANCE

10.I Corrective Maintenance

Bug fixes and error corrections performed during development:

  • Fixed cart item matching logic to handle both _id and id fields using a matchId helper function.
  • Fixed unauthenticated users being able to place orders by adding login check in Checkout.jsx with redirect to login page.
  • Fixed OTP auto-focus behavior when entering/deleting digits in the 6-box OTP input.
  • Fixed admin dashboard order polling to avoid false "new order" alerts by tracking order count with useRef.
  • Fixed HTML injection in order confirmation emails by implementing escapeHtml() for all user-provided data.

10.II Adaptive Maintenance

Changes made to adapt to new requirements and environments:

  • Added Vercel serverless deployment support (api/index.js wrapper for Express app).
  • Added CORS configuration for cross-origin API requests between frontend and backend.
  • Added environment variable support for all sensitive configurations (MongoDB URI, JWT Secret, Razorpay keys, Email credentials).
  • Added Vite proxy configuration for local development API routing.

10.III Perfective Maintenance

Performance and feature improvements:

  • Added lazy loading for menu item images with blur-to-sharp transition effect.
  • Added skeleton loading cards while menu data is being fetched.
  • Added page transitions using Framer Motion AnimatePresence for smooth navigation.
  • Added scroll-to-top behavior on route changes.
  • Added mobile-specific optimizations: bottom navigation bar, touch-friendly controls, PWA support.
  • Added real-time order polling in admin dashboard (every 3 seconds) for live updates.

10.IV Preventive Maintenance

Measures taken to prevent future issues:

  • Implemented API rate limiting to prevent brute-force attacks and server overload.
  • Added MongoDB TTL indexes for automatic OTP cleanup.
  • Added input validation on both frontend (React forms) and backend (Express routes).
  • Added error boundaries and fallback UI for failed API calls.
  • Used ESLint for code quality enforcement across the entire codebase.

12. LIMITATIONS / FUTURE SCOPE

12.I Current Limitations

  1. No Real-Time WebSocket: The current implementation uses HTTP polling (every 3 seconds) for order updates in the admin dashboard. WebSocket or Server-Sent Events would provide true real-time updates with lower server load.
  2. No Image Upload: Menu item images must be provided as URLs. There is no built-in image upload functionality. Integrating Cloudinary or AWS S3 would allow direct image uploads.
  3. Single Restaurant: The system is designed for a single restaurant. Multi-restaurant/franchise support would require schema changes and tenant isolation.
  4. No Push Notifications: The PWA has a service worker but does not implement push notifications for order updates. Web Push API integration would enhance the mobile experience.
  5. Limited Payment Options: Only Razorpay is integrated. Adding support for PayPal, Stripe, or direct UPI would increase payment flexibility.
  6. No Multi-Language Support: The interface is English-only. Adding i18n (internationalization) would make it accessible to a wider audience.
  7. Basic Analytics: The admin analytics shows basic order counts and revenue. Advanced analytics with charts, trends, and customer insights would be more useful.

12.II Future Scope

  1. WebSocket Integration: Replace HTTP polling with Socket.io for real-time order tracking, admin notifications, and live chat.
  2. AI-Powered Recommendations: Implement machine learning-based food recommendations based on user order history, preferences, and similar user behavior.
  3. Native Mobile App: Convert the PWA into a native Android/iOS application using React Native for better performance and native device features.
  4. Delivery Partner Integration: Integrate with delivery services like Dunzo, Swiggy Genie, or build an in-house delivery partner management system.
  5. Kitchen Display System: Build a dedicated kitchen display interface showing incoming orders prioritized by preparation time.
  6. Inventory Management: Add ingredient-level inventory tracking with automatic availability toggling when stock runs out.
  7. Multi-Branch Support: Extend the system to support multiple restaurant branches with centralized admin control.
  8. Voice Ordering: Integrate speech recognition for hands-free menu browsing and ordering.
  9. Customer Segmentation: Implement RFM (Recency, Frequency, Monetary) analysis for targeted marketing campaigns.
  10. A/B Testing: Add A/B testing framework for menu layouts, pricing strategies, and promotional campaigns.

COMPLETE SOURCE CODE

This section contains the complete source code of all files used in the Smart Restaurant Management System. The project consists of 113 files spanning the frontend (React.js), backend (Node.js/Express.js), database models (Mongoose), API routes, configuration files, and utility modules.

A. App.jsx -- Main Application Router

File Path: client/src/App.jsx

import { BrowserRouter as Router, Routes, Route, useLocation } from "react-router-dom"
import { useEffect } from "react"
import { motion, AnimatePresence } from "framer-motion"

import Navbar from "./components/Navbar"
import Footer from "./components/Footer"
import BottomNavbar from "./components/MobileBottomNav"
import CartDrawer from "./components/CartDrawer"
import ProtectedRoute from "./components/ProtectedRoute"
import ChatWidget from "./components/ChatWidget"
import FlashDealBanner from "./components/FlashDealBanner"

import Home from "./pages/Home"
import Menu from "./pages/Menu"
import Cart from "./pages/Cart"
import Checkout from "./pages/Checkout"
import Login from "./pages/Login"
import Register from "./pages/Register"
import Payment from "./pages/Payment"
import OrderSuccess from "./pages/OrderSuccess"
import OrderHistory from "./pages/OrderHistory"
import Profile from "./pages/Profile"
import Tracking from "./pages/Tracking"
import BookTable from "./components/BookTable"
import Favourites from "./pages/Favourites"

import AdminLogin from "./admin/AdminLogin"
import AdminDashboard from "./admin/AdminDashboard"
import AdminMenu from "./admin/AdminMenu"
import AdminCoupons from "./admin/AdminCoupons"
import AdminFlashDeals from "./admin/AdminFlashDeals"
import AdminAnalytics from "./admin/AdminAnalytics"
import AdminChat from "./admin/AdminChat"
import AdminTables from "./admin/AdminTables"

/* ── Page transition variants ── */
const pageVariants = {
  initial: { opacity: 0, y: 12 },
  animate: { opacity: 1, y: 0 },
  exit: { opacity: 0, y: -8 },
}
const pageTransition = { duration: 0.25, ease: "easeInOut" }

function PageWrap({ children }) {
  return (
    <motion.div
      variants={pageVariants}
      initial="initial"
      animate="animate"
      exit="exit"
      transition={pageTransition}
    >
      {children}
    </motion.div>
  )
}

/* ── Scroll to top on every route change ── */
function ScrollToTop() {
  const { pathname } = useLocation()
  useEffect(() => {
    window.scrollTo({ top: 0, left: 0, behavior: "instant" })
  }, [pathname])
  return null
}

/* ── Animated Routes ── */
function AnimatedRoutes() {
  const location = useLocation()
  return (
    <AnimatePresence mode="wait">
      <Routes location={location} key={location.pathname}>
        {/* Customer Routes */}
        <Route path="/" element={<PageWrap><Home /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/menu" element={<PageWrap><Menu /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/cart" element={<PageWrap><Cart /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/checkout" element={<PageWrap><Checkout /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/login" element={<PageWrap><Login /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/register" element={<PageWrap><Register /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/payment" element={<PageWrap><Payment /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/success" element={<PageWrap><OrderSuccess /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/orders" element={<PageWrap><OrderHistory /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/profile" element={<PageWrap><Profile /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/tracking" element={<PageWrap><Tracking /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/book-table" element={<PageWrap><BookTable /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/favourites" element={<PageWrap><Favourites /></PageWrap>} />

        {/* Admin Routes */}
        <Route path="/admin-login" element={<PageWrap><AdminLogin /></PageWrap>} />
        <Route path="/admin" element={
          <ProtectedRoute>
            <PageWrap><AdminDashboard /></PageWrap>
          </ProtectedRoute>
        } />
        <Route path="/admin-menu" element={
          <ProtectedRoute>
            <PageWrap><AdminMenu /></PageWrap>
          </ProtectedRoute>
        } />
        <Route path="/admin-coupons" element={
          <ProtectedRoute>
            <PageWrap><AdminCoupons /></PageWrap>
          </ProtectedRoute>
        } />
        <Route path="/admin-flash-deals" element={
          <ProtectedRoute>
            <PageWrap><AdminFlashDeals /></PageWrap>
          </ProtectedRoute>
        } />
        <Route path="/admin-analytics" element={
          <ProtectedRoute>
            <PageWrap><AdminAnalytics /></PageWrap>
          </ProtectedRoute>
        } />
        <Route path="/admin-chat" element={
          <ProtectedRoute>
            <PageWrap><AdminChat /></PageWrap>
          </ProtectedRoute>
        } />
        <Route path="/admin-tables" element={
          <ProtectedRoute>
            <PageWrap><AdminTables /></PageWrap>
          </ProtectedRoute>
        } />
      </Routes>
    </AnimatePresence>
  )
}

function AppLayout() {
  const location = useLocation()

  // Hide customer navbar/footer on admin pages
  const isAdminPage = location.pathname.startsWith("/admin")
  const isHomePage = location.pathname === "/"

  return (
    <>
      {/* Scroll to top on navigation */}
      <ScrollToTop />

      {/* Flash Deal Banner - only on customer pages */}
      {!isAdminPage && <FlashDealBanner />}

      {/* Top Navbar - only on customer pages */}
      {!isAdminPage && <Navbar />}

      {/* Page Content — no top padding on homepage (hero goes behind navbar) */}
      <div className={isAdminPage ? "min-h-screen" : isHomePage ? "min-h-screen" : "pt-14 sm:pt-20 min-h-screen"}>
        <AnimatedRoutes />
      </div>

      {/* Footer & Mobile Nav - only on customer pages */}
      {!isAdminPage && <Footer />}
      {!isAdminPage && <BottomNavbar />}

      {/* Cart Drawer - only on customer pages */}
      {!isAdminPage && <CartDrawer />}

      {/* Live Chat Widget - only on customer pages */}
      {!isAdminPage && <ChatWidget />}
    </>
  )
}

export default function App() {
  return (
    <Router>
      <AppLayout />
    </Router>
  )
}
